<div id="review_1294232304" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1294232304" />
    <a title="Wendy&#39;sThoughts" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17755575-wendy-sthoughts"><img alt="Wendy&#39;sThoughts" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1378340325p2/17755575.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1294232304?book_show_action=true">May 30, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wendy&#39;sThoughts" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wendy&#39;sThoughts" href="/user/show/17755575-wendy-sthoughts">Wendy&#39;sThoughts</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Soccer Fans, Sport, Mariana Zapata Fans</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Wendy'sThoughts by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/11856352-mo">Mo</a>
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1294232304" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5800034380922440557"><b>5 Schnecke Stars <br/>* * * * * and any other you may want to personally add! <i>Spoiler Free </i><br/>I have started this review a few times since reading; had a review halfway done and then in editing lost it- What else is new- you have all heard it before... The next time I sat and just thought about all of the amazing feelings and memories this book brought home to me. <br/><br/>Before I go into my personal review, please take a moment to read the reviews which brought me to this amazing reading experience. The follow</b></span>
  <span id="freeText5800034380922440557" style="display:none"><b>5 Schnecke Stars <br>* * * * * and any other you may want to personally add! <i>Spoiler Free </i><br>I have started this review a few times since reading; had a review halfway done and then in editing lost it- What else is new- you have all heard it before... The next time I sat and just thought about all of the amazing feelings and memories this book brought home to me. <br><br>Before I go into my personal review, please take a moment to read the reviews which brought me to this amazing reading experience. The following reviews en-capsule all of the feelings and intensity of emotions one can feel after reading this. These reviews by Mo and Didi started my desire to read Kulti. <br><br>Here is Mo's Review:<br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1291106173?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a><br>Here is Didi's Review:<br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1238827071?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a><br><br>In talking about this book, as I mentioned before posting today, it is the type of book you will either throw yourself into or not...It is not the usual romance of love/hate and then boom they look at each other and HEA lust etc... There is so much to this because it is surrounded by a story that highlights so much about women's lives in Sport; Sport itself or anything you dedicated your whole life to achieve. It is all of this focus, determination, understanding of what is important and finally, learning to stand up and look out for the one who is the most important in these types of pursuits... the person who is doing all of this... You. <br><br>These types of ideas and themes cannot be told in a vacuum...and Mariana Zapata created this story as if it were made out of 100 layers of filo dough for the finest, sweet yet tart pastry ever. </b><br><br>Our main gal, Sal, is part of an amazing family in so many ways. It has the warmth, history and understanding of not being perfect but unique; unique in the ways sport families are- supportive, understanding of what is needed to have the children excel and willing to sacrifice in order for the talent to grow. The father is a Football/Futbol/Soccer fan; her older brother showed talent early and was on his way when Sal at six started to become interested, too. Mother wished for other sports for her first daughter making her take karate and swimming as part of the deal to do Soccer. Yet Soccer was the passion and language which bonded Sal to her father the most...laying a foundation which became so strong... they were equally best friends as well as father and daughter as they both matured over the years. <br><br>We learn of the turning point for Sal which will guide her throughout her life and career. It was the Atus Cup Semi-Final between Spain and Germany. This match happens every three years and is the most-watched event in the world. It looks as if Germany has no chance to come back and win. The family is watching on their TV and outcomes one of the last players allowed for Germany. He is this lanky, teenage man/child who approaches the field with no fear or apprehension, no concern of never playing at this International level in such a crucial game before... No... he came to win his body and attitude said.....and he did. He played like he was unbeatable; ruthless and at the end performed like no other. <br><br>In those moments of joy in her family's home, Sal saw what all that could mean and feel like... to cause strangers to be united in Joy and Spirit...<br><br>It showed her that anything was possible...<br>That you could do what no one believed you could do...<br><br><b> Seven-year-old Sal had her epiphany and from that moment on she knew 2 things:<br><br>She was going to make others feel the same way one day because Soccer was going to be what she was going to do...<br><br>And <br><br>Reiner Kulti and her were going to marry and have wonderful Soccer loving babies together.</b> <br><br>Well, part of her dream was in the making; at 27, Sal was playing for the Houston Pipers and had been instrumental in the team's championship-winning season... They put her front and center in the mural on the wall of the entrance. She had been with the team going on 4 years now and was regarded well by her teammates and coach. She had learned patience and understanding from her father's lessons of "pulling up her big girl socks" and to attack the things she feared... to make herself do them even through the fear. In other words, she was a remarkable woman.<br><br>She had lived through all the years of training; pushing herself when others would relax. She knew what she wanted and did not let others dictate how she saw herself. She was comfortable with her strong and able body; she knew her routines of running every morning 5 miles put her ahead in the training bank... making her the fastest and best on the field. She put up with her mother's wanting her to be someone she wasn't when the comments came of her putting on a little makeup or dress would be a way for her to "find" someone. She knew her mother meant no harm... it was just her way. She even allowed her baby sister to ignore her at times...understanding she felt left out by her dislike of all sport.<br><br>She also had the ability to try to let go of all the political and personal hurts she had experienced over the years. It was part of the journey; but they hurt and under minded more than the physical pain. She had worked through the most recent disappointment of not being on the National Team due to no fault of her own....just being a pawn in circumstances not of her choosing.<br><br>So as she listens to her coach tell her she is needed to be part of a press conference (something which makes her suffer from such intense stage fright she has shakes, nausea and a mouth that acts on its own), she only hears him say, "and Reiner Kulti is going to be the new assistant coach, so that is why the press."<br><br>Noooooooooooooo....As the rest of the words are sounding like Waaa Waaa from the Charlie Brown cartoon, all Sal can think about is this cannot be happening.<br><br>Her 13-year-old self was heartbroken when Kulti, Soccer Icon, married an actress/model. It hurt and was something which took quite some time to get over even though the marriage ended months after. He then almost destroyed her brother's career during a game. How was she going to handle being in the same room, let alone having to talk and work with him....<br><br>After a disastrous press conference with the only saving grace being Kulti was a no show, Sal knows she has to buckle down and figure out how to deal with this situation. She talks with her dad, who idolizes Kulti even after what he did to her brother. He guides her to understanding these things happen in sport and to just move on. He gives her encouragement as always in his way they have with each other and she is better.<br><br><b>Side Note-</b> <i>The relationship she has with her father is one of the most heartwarming in my reading experience. Through all of Sal's interactions with him, they reminded me of mine with my Dad. My Dad was a force; he had this ability to talk with anyone and have them feel he was sincerely interested. I have memories after memories of times where we would experience things never anticipated because of his curiosity and willingness to engage. The way Sal's father talks and shares with her brings all of that back.</i><br><br>The other thing which Sal decides to use is the age-old trick of thinking of something universal to all humans no matter the talent or icon status:<br><br>Poop...yes, that wonderful method to bring all people down to the level they need to be on...We all do it... so by that reasoning...no one is more special than any other...It is a tool she uses to allow her to be on the same field and not make a fool of herself...<br><br>Now to the idea of Reiner Kulti- this is a man who is in a situation of his making but not because he wishes to be there. He has regrets and now he is here as an assistant coaching for an American Women's Soccer team. He could be with any other team on any other continent. He is a man of few words, documented with a terrible temper, and one of the most talented players ever. He is hiding secrets and Sal senses there is more to all of this.<br><br>So the set up of our gal having her obsession for so many years be her assistant coach and how she handles it is the major part. We see the interaction of the two of them... her having to help him out of a sticky situation to begin with...then it continues when she confronts his rudeness to her father during a fan event. It is a turning point for Kulti and then the level of contact between them changes- they become careful friends. <br><br>There is more, though. We see how Sal must battle jealousy, unmerited gossip, and the pain of being an athlete. She is focused and easy in her life having her family as a support system with two close teammates as personal friends and her business partner.<br><br>We see how women who work just as hard in Sport are not nearly as compensated or respected as their counterparts. How most, unless having means, need outside jobs in order to support themselves. <br><br>What we experience overall is the growth of a Stubborn German to become more humane and his critical influence in instilling more confidence and performance in Sal. There is so much more but I shall allow you to discover it. <br><br>I would be remiss if I didn't mention the wonderful humor woven seamlessly in every scene. The banter and cutting wit of Sal is perfection. One of the delights was hearing all the names she calls this man, in her head as well as out loud to his face.<br><br>So to sum up my love of this book- take it as it is given...it tells the true story of Professional Sport in America for Women; gives insight to the type of drive needed to succeed in Sport as well as any pursuit; there is romance and allows us to experience that anything is possible...<br><br><b> Before Review but After Reading</b><br>What is important about this book are the feelings you may have ... if you allow yourself to feel them. <br><br>This is not a quick ramp-up to romance... this is entirely different and some may love it and others may feel it is not their cuppa- but for me...<br><br>It brought so many memories and feelings to the surface... it just worked. <br><br>I need to edit my thoughts with this one... because if I don't the review will go on and on :D :D<br><br> <br><strong>For more Reviews, Free E-books and Giveaways</strong><br><div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1558049022?book_show_action=true">Feb 23, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wendy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wendy" href="/user/show/32445724-wendy">Wendy</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1558049022" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13509692109689308090">Re-read again still absolutely love the shit out of this book and I still have a major girl crush going on ;) <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1503222915i/23640369._SX540_.jpg' alt='5-stars-640x162.jpg (640×162)' width='242' height='61' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1456431928ra/18234425.gif' alt=' photo post-26228-Up-Boy-WOW-gif-Imgur-xKwN_zpsrgbda7jt.gif' width='313' height='176' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I can honestly say that this book has been the best I've read this year so far !! It was absolutely awesome. It's hard for me to explain why I loved it so much. Maybe it was the great writing style. It could also be, because of the amazing characters. I loved Sal and Kulti, but I also really Sal's father and her friends. The character build was really good.<br/><br/>One of the other reasons I love</span>
  <span id="freeText13509692109689308090" style="display:none">Re-read again still absolutely love the shit out of this book and I still have a major girl crush going on ;) <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1503222915i/23640369._SX540_.jpg" alt="5-stars-640x162.jpg (640×162)" width="242" height="61" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1456431928ra/18234425.gif" alt=" photo post-26228-Up-Boy-WOW-gif-Imgur-xKwN_zpsrgbda7jt.gif" width="313" height="176" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I can honestly say that this book has been the best I've read this year so far !! It was absolutely awesome. It's hard for me to explain why I loved it so much. Maybe it was the great writing style. It could also be, because of the amazing characters. I loved Sal and Kulti, but I also really Sal's father and her friends. The character build was really good.<br><br>One of the other reasons I loved this book is : <strong>SOCCER</strong>. I am from the Netherlands, and we are all about soccer. It was really refreshing for me, to finally read a book about a sport that I know really well !!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1503222915ra/23640370.gif" alt="tenor.gif (220×220)" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I wasn't bored for a second and that is impressing because this book is pretty long !!<br><br>It also made me pee my pants laughing....damn the heroine, she was so freaking funny :)) She is definitely one of my all-time favorite heroines. I absolutely adored Salome !! I wanted to be her new best friend...I might have a huge girl crush going on :P<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1503222915ra/23640371.gif" alt="tumblr_m6bdgzWSW81qczdezo1_250.gif (245×185)" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So what is it about...<br><br>It's about a girl who grew up to be a professional soccer player. Her brother is also a professional player and her dad is her biggest fan. She grew up watching Reiner Kulti (a famous German player) on tv and decided she wanted to be him...and marry him. Of course reality got in the way of her dreams because when she was 17, he married someone else. He was 13 years older and she had never met him in person, but it still broke her 17-year-old delusional heart :(<br><br><strong>“It was the worst non-break-up ever in the history of imaginary relationships with a man who didn't even know I existed.” </strong><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1503222915ra/23640372.gif" alt="“You get one free pass.” – Scandal Gif-Cap" width="400" height="204" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Still, she focused on playing and being the best...which isn't as easy being a girl, playing a sport mostly played by men. She is a very nice girl, she has a nice set of balls on the field, but she is still very much a good girl.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1503222915ra/23640373.gif" alt="soccer uswnt alex morgan womens world cup woso GIF" width="333" height="186" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>When she is 27, her coach lets her know that they've hired a new assistant coach..... non-other than Reiner Kulti. At that time, Sal doesn't know how she feels about this. Her 17-year-old heart is still broken and pissed, but she is also angry at him because of a soccer incident that happened between him and her brother. On the other hand, he has always been her idol and her reason for playing soccer in the first place. Also, her dad absolutely idolizes Kulti.<br><br>So she sucks up all her negative feelings and decides to just go with it. She would love to learn something from the best. Turns out the best is a freaking asshole !! He made more than one mistake and Sal finally has enough and can't take any more of his shit. She blows...which ironically is the start of an amazing friendship :))<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1503222915ra/23640374.gif" alt="hello hi wave hey welcome GIF" width="163" height="152" class="gr-hostedUserImg">   <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1503222915ra/23640375.gif" alt="tumblr_os9vebOWyp1sov4w6o1_500.gif (500×500)" width="150" height="150" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I'm not gonna say anymore, just that I loved every page of this one. This Bratwurst and Taco were great together. The banter between them had me in stitches.<br><br>Now I will say, don't go into this one thinking it will be all romance and steam.....To be honest, the steam takes a very very long time...For me, someone who absolutely loves steam, it wasn't a problem. Which says a lot :) The way their relationship grew and how they became friends and finally more than friends was absolutely swoon-worthy to me<br><br>.<img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1503222915i/23640376.jpg" alt="tumblr_inline_o1fbcsri6I1tsdqet_540.jpg (300×188)" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><em>
  <strong>“You are my equal, my partner, my teammate, my best friend.”</strong>
</em><br><br>I am sure I will read this book many many times over. It was that freaking awesome! This one definitely goes in my "all-time" top 10 of mf books.<br><br><a href="http://s172.photobucket.com/user/Wendy_Ciliacus/media/100_s_zpsxfwwoudc.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1456431928ra/18234426.gif" alt=" photo 100_s_zpsxfwwoudc.gif" width="353" height="159" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I would love to give it 10 stars...but I can only give 5, so that's what it will be !!</span>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1306715093" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6349915790808166507"><b>5 **<u>Fußball</u>** STARS</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1454678613i/17998993.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“He was my coach. And I was his friend. Or something like that.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><br/>What a fantastic read. A phenomenally written friends to lovers story surrounding a female soccer player and her new coach - a retired professional player, an icon and he is German. If you don't know, that happens to be my nationality and we like our football. So it was a foregone conclusion that I would love this just because of the premise alone. Add to that a brilliantly developed friendship, top no</span>
  <span id="freeText6349915790808166507" style="display:none"><b>5 **<u>Fußball</u>** STARS</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1454678613i/17998993.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“He was my coach. And I was his friend. Or something like that.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>What a fantastic read. A phenomenally written friends to lovers story surrounding a female soccer player and her new coach - a retired professional player, an icon and he is German. If you don't know, that happens to be my nationality and we like our football. So it was a foregone conclusion that I would love this just because of the premise alone. Add to that a brilliantly developed friendship, top notch bickering and fighting and a once in a lifetime love story. I was a gonner.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1418911509i/12944326.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Every single thing that has ever happened in my life has led me here, Sal. Destiny is a ladder, a series of steps that takes you where you’re supposed to go. I am the man that I am, and I have done the things that I’ve done, to get me to you.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>A little more about the story. Twenty-seven year old <b>Sal Casillas</b> always had a crush on now thirty-nine year old <b>Reiner Kulti</b>, her icon and the player and man who made her want to be the athlete she is today. The childhood crush is long gone, but he is still someone she holds dear to her heart. Imagine the surprise when he comes to Houston to be the new assistant coach. <br><br>They say, you never should meet your idols, right? Well, it turns out Kulti is a grumpy and silent guy, with a boatload of issues, who couldn't care less about his surroundings, or even teaching the girls anything. Really a disappointment and it doesn't take long for the strong willed Sal to clash with the man of her past dreams. You could say it is an enemy - to friends - to lovers story.<br><br>If nothing else <i>Kulti</i> is a slow burn. For everyone who hates insta-love, this might be just the book. A realistically developed relationship with a lot of ups and downs. A very detailed look into the world of women's soccer and the politics behind it. Enjoyable, addictive and heartwarming.<br><br>If you are interested to know, the author didn't butcher my mother tongue. She didn't use German all that much, but a lot of endearments and the odd phrase here and there was right on point. I really appreciate actual research when using another language. ;)<br><br><br><i>And just because...here is a fun fact. Superbowl 2014 - 111.5 Mio viewers. Viewers of the final match of the ‘soccer’ World Cup in 2010 - 909.6 Mio. You tell me which one is the real football. Just sayin'.</i><br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1418911509i/12944326.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a href="http://coffeeaddictbooks.blogspot.co.at/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1447539995i/17017465.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="https://www.facebook.com/coffeeaddictbooks?ref=tn_tnmn" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1431598100i/14852514.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1654757701" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1654757701" />
    <a title="sraxe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6378079-sraxe"><img alt="sraxe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1449303386p2/6378079.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1654757701?book_show_action=true">May 31, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="sraxe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="sraxe" href="/user/show/6378079-sraxe">sraxe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6378079-sraxe?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6378079-sraxe?shelf=1-star">1-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6378079-sraxe?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6378079-sraxe?shelf=heroine-non-virginal">heroine-non-virginal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6378079-sraxe?shelf=poc">poc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6378079-sraxe?shelf=br-urr">br-urr</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6378079-sraxe?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6378079-sraxe?shelf=friends-to-lovers">friends-to-lovers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6378079-sraxe?shelf=written-review">written-review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6378079-sraxe?shelf=first-person">first-person</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1654757701" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9812124774830093800">I love slow burn novels. When a novel builds up to the eventual consummation, I feel it's so much sweeter. That's why I'm disappointed with how much I disliked this. While it picks up in the second half, it's hard to forget how the first half dragged and felt like a chore. In the end, the pay-off felt sub-par at best. I needed something a bit more spectacular after enduring pages of food names and "poop" (both of which would've been funny in moderation, but were killed with overuse), "the German</span>
  <span id="freeText9812124774830093800" style="display:none">I love slow burn novels. When a novel builds up to the eventual consummation, I feel it's so much sweeter. That's why I'm disappointed with how much I disliked this. While it picks up in the second half, it's hard to forget how the first half dragged and felt like a chore. In the end, the pay-off felt sub-par at best. I needed something a bit more spectacular after enduring pages of food names and "poop" (both of which would've been funny in moderation, but were killed with overuse), "the German," and other irritating things.<br /><br />(Note: It's hard to talk about this book and my issues without spoilers. Due to length and pace, I'm not sure what would and wouldn't qualify as a spoiler, so beware of unmarked spoilers below.)<br /><br />As said, this book is super slow burn. Kulti doesn't show up until halfway through Chapter Three. After finally touching—shaking hands—at just over 10%, nothing happens for a while. He's quiet and stand-offish, while Sal watches him from afar. Around 20%, something finally happens when she confronts him for being an ass. After that, he sullenly interacts with her and they slowly start becoming friends 50% in. They don't kiss until the 85% mark, with sex not happening until past the 90% point. NBD, right? It wouldn't be...if the book wasn't nearly 500 PAGES LONG. While it's nice that Zapata took time to develop things, the pay-off with the not-so-great written sex scenes, that felt really rushed and included by force, were extremely inadequate for all that build-up. Then it also became the story of Special Snowflake Sal, with her famous footballer grandfather, Kulti joining the Pipers because of Sal, and how he still has her childhood letters to him.<br /><br />The reason why this book is so long is because Zapata kept throwing in subplots. Not bad in and of itself, but it is when they're never fully realized. Rather than sticking to one thing and developing that completely, Zapata was adding a ton of subplots. Each subplot also felt like its own mini episode in the book, being introduced and a part of the story for a time (usually a chapter, maybe two) before it's dropped.<br /><br />And when I mean not fully realized, I mean that I was left with a ton of questions by the end and subplots that were shallowly explored, even important things. Nearly 500 pages, and we never know why Kulti's marriage ended. Hell, I don't even think his ex-wife's name is mentioned ONCE or why he ever married her. When Kulti starts hitching rides with Sal, where was his driver? What was up with Sal's ankle in the beginning? What was up with the uncle who wanted tickets to a game? What did Grace and Kulti fight about? Why was Kulti so angry on the phone when he was speaking in German? Who the hell is Mike Walton? Why were the softball players purposely hurting Sal? Why did Kulti get his tattoo covered up? What did the old one mean? What was Cecy's problem? Etc. (There're probably others that I missed, but that's all I'm recalling for the moment.)<br /><br />Just WAY TOO MANY subplots.<br /><br />While there were tons of unnecessary things, important ones were left out. Like Eric. Sal keeps mentioning how close she is to her brother and how they talk often, yet he never makes an appearance in the entire book? She mentions two calls with him, but they're recounted after the fact and skimmed over. How you gonna tell me that Eric is the sibling she's closest to, yet it's Cecy who makes more appearances in the book than him? Even Eric's bffs are in the book while he isn't. (Not surprising, I guess. Near the end when Kulti's sitting with her parents, she thinks that they're the three people she loves most in the world. Wtf happened to that brother you were supposedly ~so close~ to, Sal?)<br /><br />And what destroyed Sal's adolescent love for Kulti was that he got married and then nearly ended her brother's career. Two things that had such an impact on her Kulti obsession, but neither make an appearance in this book. (Also, that move that Kulti pulled that nearly ended Eric's career? Was it a dirty move on his part? An accident? What? Zapata makes a BFD about it in the beginning but it fades into the background and it's then forgotten.)<br /><br />Then there's the fact that Zapata has a tendency to be repetitive. She repeats so many things, like blinking, Kulti's height, Sal tipping her head to talk to him, scratching her cheek, biting the inside of her cheek, "Big Girl Socks," the length and colour of Kulti's hair, etc. She also mentions Kulti's eyes an insane amount of times, changing it up to different colours: hazel, hazel-green, green, green-brown, "light-colored," "perfect shade between green-green and hazel-brown," green-moss, jewel-like, clear eyes, amber, swamp colored. I'm sure there were some I missed, but even without those, this is INSANE. First, wtf does "light-colored" even mean?! And second, how can he have "light-colored" and "swamp colored" eyes??<br /><br />Sal also has OTT reactions to Kulti, even weeks into their friendship. It's fine at first, but when she's thinking "Dear God, Reiner Kulti was hugging the shit out of me. I just stood there with my arms at my sides, frozen. Completely freaking frozen in place. I was stunned, beyond stunned. Stupefied" AFTER she's already spent a weekend with him, shared a bunk, seen him in his underwear, and had her parent's lawn mowed by him, it's a bit much. And whenever Kulti would walk into a new place or do something "normal" and she's thinking <i>"Reiner 'The King' Kulti" was doing blah blah blah or in such-and-such a place! Unbelievable!</i> 90% and she's thinking "I was sitting in the backseat of a car with Reiner ‘The King’ Kulti on the way to the WPL final game, asking him if he was still going to love me once I couldn’t play anymore. Good God." CHILL THE FUCK OUT, GIRL.<br /><br />There were also a ton of mistakes that other readers have noted, like and insane amount of comma abuse and misuse and other errors. Oh, and there was the scene when Kulti and Sal are finally kissing.<br /><br /><blockquote>I tilted my head back, my throat completely exposed as I sighed in desperation. ... I shut my mouth and gave him an exasperated look. ... He tilted his face down, making sure our eyes were meeting. All I could manage to do was stare and hyperventilate. ... I could feel my lower lip trembling as his thumbs rubbed the tender part in the crook of my elbow. ... Kulti tipped his head down, eye to eye like he’d been with me when I’d woken up from my concussion. ... Those big hands left my thighs and before I could wonder where they were going, they landed on my cheeks. In a split second, he tilted my face just slightly down and we were eye to eye, his breath on my face.</blockquote><br />He keeps tilting and tipping his head down (or hers up/back), their eyes keep meeting even though there's no mention of either of them having turned away or broken eye contact. His hands go from being on her elbow to her thighs. While I should be savouring the scene, I was too distracted by the mistakes. How do you make this many mistakes in such an important scene?<br /><br />What this book needed was an editor to cleave, tighten, and clean the plot. Did it have one? With all the mistakes riddling the book, I can't be sure. If it did, Zapata clearly needs someone better.<br /><br />With the story itself, there were a number of things that bothered me. The age difference, for one (13 years in this case). I'm not a fan of May-December relationships, particularly if hero is the older one. I found it adorable in the beginning because we've all had those celebrity infatuations, but I was a little worried because I thought it would go from her being a kid and hero-worshipping him, to being an adult and him taking advantage of said worship and nostalgia. As the story progressed and she dealt with his disinterest and assholery, I liked that she became disillusioned. I liked that the relationship was broken down before being built back up.<br /><br />HOWEVER, that was before the reveal that she'd loved him all along! (Sorry, but I don't buy Zapata trying to push a childhood infatuation with a celebrity as REAL LOVE ALL ALONG.) Then, it's revealed that Kulti had been aware of Sal's infatuation with him. In fact, he says that he still has the letters she sent him when she was SEVEN YEAR OLD KID. He has them FRAMED in his house. Sure, that's adorable...but not when you fucking pair them up as romantic interests! And then he goes on about how they were ALWAYS MEANT TO BE TOGETHER and everything he did in his life led him to her. What the FUCK. I was so creeped out! This dude is telling her that he has her letters from when she was 7 (and he was 19-20) framed in his house and OH LOOK TRUE LOVE.<br /><br /><blockquote>"Every single thing that has ever happened in my life has led me here, Sal. Destiny is a ladder, a series of steps that takes you where you’re supposed to go. I am the man that I am, and I have done the things that I’ve done, to get me to you."</blockquote><br />NOT romantic when you're talking about their earliest interactions being when she was a kid and he was into adulthood! What're they gonna tell their kids? "See this frame right here, kids? This is the letter your mom sent me when she was seven! Oh, and over here! The three others she sent me, too!"<br /><br />This was why I gave it a 1. Before this, I was around a 2 because, while I didn't think it was great, I didn't feel it was super awful, either. BUT, then Zapata was pushing this true love/destiny BS at the end, and then combined with the age difference and how he still kept her letters, it was just too creepy for me. Oh, and it didn't make sense.<br /><br />How? If he knew ALL ALONG that she was his #1 fan, that he came to the team simply because of her, and that he STILL has her letters framed in his house...why did he treat her like shit in the beginning of the book? Why did he threaten to bench her after she helped him? Why did he do ANY of that in the beginning? It simply makes no sense to me.<br /><br />Another issue was Kulti's DUI. Others didn't have an issue, but it was something that bothered me throughout. Upon first learning about his possible DUI, Sal immediately decides that "[she] wasn't disappointed" because "things like that were more luck-based than anything. ... How many people didn’t drive home after having a few drinks? Sometimes you got caught and most times you didn’t. Whatever." Later, she tells him that "[he] didn’t steal anything or kill anyone. Whatever anyone else who doesn’t know [him] thinks, isn’t a big deal."<br /><br />Look, it's not that I think that he should be forever condemned by a bad decision, it's that I hate Zapata's dismissive attitude towards it. Sal's immediate thoughts are about him getting caught, not whether or not people may been hurt, so "whatever." Then she implies theft is worse. (Yes, because that one library book I kinda sorta stole years ago makes me more worthy of being judged than if I ever got behind the wheel of a car intoxicated, right?) At a certain point, she even offers her car up to him. Because lending your car to someone with a suspended license is a super great idea.<br /><br />During the book, his DUI is glossed over and there are no real answers. There's no definitive on whether someone got hurt or anything else about it. We're not even told how he got caught. (Was he pulled over? A random checkpoint? An accident?) Instead, Zapata consistently frames it sympathetically in his favour. Even Sal, before knowing ANYTHING about the situation, is immediately forgiving, saying it's "whatever" and "we all make mistakes." There's no accountability on his part and how someone could've gotten hurt, even him.<br /><br />And I do legit mean that there's no responsibility taken by him. When he finally does open up, he only says that "[he] was in a bad place after [he] retired," picking up a bad habit he's not proud of due to his anger at the time. That's it. He doesn't talk about how reckless it was, that he could've hurt others or himself, or the hundred different other things. Instead, Zapata portrays him as the sympathetic party in the situation. At this time, Sal thinks that "people made mistakes all the time. He had a right to make them as much as the next person." Even though she still doesn't know jack about any of the details in regards to his DUI.<br /><br />Seriously though...am I supposed to feel bad that a rich, privileged celebrity like Kulti is facing consequences for his actions? He may have been going through a tough time, but so what? It's not that I feel he's undeserving of human compassion, it's that he NEVER takes responsibility for his actions. He has his DUI and gets his license suspended and then he continues to bury it. When he finally does admit that he had a DUI? He gives a sob story as an excuse for what he did but with no accountability. Hell, when he tells Sal, he doesn't say that he's not proud of getting behind the wheel drunk, he just says he's not proud of the habit he picked up, which was drinking. I can't feel bad for someone who doesn't acknowledge their own wrong doing. Telling me that you were in a tough place isn't taking responsibility, that's absolving yourself of blame. (And this is not even getting into how his fame, being "one of the best players in the world, ever," probably gained him clemency.)<br /><br />What I wanted was a simple acknowledgement of his poor decisions, which could easily be done. You can call out someone's problematic behaviours without thinking the person is the scum of the earth. If we were to condemn every person over something problematic, we'd never be able to support anyone. But, that doesn't mean you can't dislike what they did. And I felt that Zapata did a disservice by concentrating on how the DUI had an effect on him rather than the possible fatal repercussions. Sal didn't even need to dog-pile; she could've just felt disappointment in his actions. Except, to her, it's just a "mistake" and "people made mistakes all the time" and "whatever." Yes, people make mistakes and bad decisions, but it doesn't help if you baby them! Kulti is a grown fucking man of nearly forty!<br /><br />And besides, Sal seems to have a double standard when it comes to condemnation.<br /><br />While she doesn't judge Kulti, she's quick to jump on Amber. After Gardner tells her about an anonymous letter, she immediately blames Amber, calling her "that bitch. That fucking bitch." At this point, Sal has absolutely NO EVIDENCE to believe that it was actually her. With Kulti, she holds back on judging him, even after she does find out that he did have a DUI. With this anonymous letter, she immediately blames Amber. And besides, all she knows about it is that it contains "wild accusations" and nothing more. While it probably was Amber, she can't be sure. What about all the anti-fan mail she's been getting? How can she be sure it wasn't one of them?<br /><br />Oh, Sal can believe it's her because Amber recently called her a whore? Well, what about believing that Kulti might have a DUI because she had to drag his ass out of a bar? If one leads her to make an assumption about the other in Amber's case, why does she refrain from doing so in Kulti's? She's not even friendly with him at this point.<br /><br />Is it because Amber threatened her career? Well, Kulti did too, remember? When she did him a favour and dragged his drunk ass to a hotel room and he repaid her the next day by threatening to bench her if she gossiped? Remember that, Sal? While Amber's influence is periphery with Sal's career now, Kulti's is direct. Not only does Kulti hold a position of power, but his celebrity further amplifies that in terms of overall sway.<br /><br />Later, Sal refers to Amber as having a "whiny black heart." Uh...have you met Kulti? At least Amber had something legitimate to be upset about. What about Kulti's whining? While Amber is a "bitch" because of presumed actions, Kulti gets a shrug and a "shit happens" response. I dunno...I tend to feel that someone who DUIs and doesn't take responsibility might have more of a "black heart" than someone who's holding a grudge because you got caught dating their husband. But maybe that's just me.<br /><br />I was really annoyed at the marked difference in how she treats Kulti's behaviour in comparison to everyone else. Amber gets the <i>this bitch, that bitch, bitchbitchbitch</i> treatment while Kulti gets the <i>ohhh you poor baby!!</i> one.<br /><br />Anyway.<br /><br />One of the times I agreed with Sal was when she said she was anti-manwhore. It was a nice change...and then she hooked up with Kulti, who'd been around. I thought her anti-manwhore bit might lead to a reveal about Kulti's dating past being exaggerated, but that didn't happen. I wouldn't mind Kulti's past so much if there weren't such a disparity in their experience. Not only does she mention only one boyfriend, but when she's with Kulti, she notes that "it was more visual memory from the hundreds of soft-core porn movies [she]’d occasionally caught on late night cable that reminded [her] what to do" because she hasn't had sex in "a long, long time." Kulti's been celibate for a year. But honestly? That doesn't mean much to me when he was probably a manwhore for two decades.<br /><br />Then there's the paparazzi. Zapata makes a BFD about how they're all over Kulti, which is made worse after news of his DUI and rumours about Sal. You'd think they'd always be around, right? While the paparazzi will follow them to some random doctor's clinic, no one catches Sal giving daily rides home to Kulti after games? These two can stand outside the stadium post-game and shout at each other, but there's no news of that? Kulti kisses her outside the stadium post-media shitstorm, and no one papped them? I didn't like how the paparazzi was conveniently there and then not.<br /><br />Zapata should've also done more research with football. One glaring mistake was when, during a league finals championship match, Sal got two yellow cards! Unless the rules are different for Zapata's football, Sal should've been thrown from the match. Also, while it might be fine for Sal to use "soccer" because she's American, it doesn't make sense for Kulti, seeing as how he was born, raised, and played in Europe all his life. Zapata also says that league teams here were referred to as "teams" (as opposed to "clubs"). Uh...they're still called clubs in North America. New York City FC and Toronto FC are both MLS football clubs. Zapata may have confused it with how national teams are titled teams (USMNT), but that, too, follows Europe's footsteps and how they're called "teams" on the international level. An average person can be excused for not knowing this, but not Zapata. This is the main theme of her book and she should have done her research.<br /><br />Then there's sexist, slut-shaming Sal. She refers to some Kulti fangirls as "hookers." Sure, she follows this with "that wasn’t very nice," but then why even include it? Besides, Sal's an obsessed fan herself who was star-struck and internally fangirling over Kulti SO MUCH. Also, I don't believe the "that wasn't very nice" because she later refers to her teammates as whores. This is after they stop getting along, but did she have to resort to that? Besides, at a point earlier, she was upset at being called that because she totally wasn't ("Getting called a whore? Especially when you weren’t one? Yeah, it wasn’t exactly fun and games."), so why would she think of other women that way? Then Kulti's ex makes an appearance and Sal considers her desperate-looking. Why did Zapata even bother including her? Simply to disparage another woman? The woman isn't even given a name! Kulti just ignores her like a douche and then she's gone. And lastly, mention of how he's dated "sluts ("The man, who had dated supermodels, actresses and probably a whole bunch of sluts."). I mean...if there's a slut in this equation, it's the man you're referring to as having dated a shit-ton of women.<br /><br />Overall, just not an enjoyable experience.<br /><br />(This was read as a buddy-read with the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/187063" rel="nofollow noopener">Unapologetic Romance Readers</a> group.)</span>
  <a data-text-id="9812124774830093800" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2732822102" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2732822102" />
    <a title="♥ℂĦℝΪՖƬΪℕÅ" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52207144"><img alt="♥ℂĦℝΪՖƬΪℕÅ" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568965358p2/52207144.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2732822102?book_show_action=true">Mar 15, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="♥ℂĦℝΪՖƬΪℕÅ" class="user" itemprop="url" name="♥ℂĦℝΪՖƬΪℕÅ" href="/user/show/52207144">♥ℂĦℝΪՖƬΪℕÅ</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781494562724" href="/book/show/26459239-kulti">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52207144?shelf=2019-reading-challenge">2019-reading-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52207144?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52207144?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52207144?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2732822102" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2771322427762954777"><b>
  <u>3 German Chocolate Cake ★'s</u>
</b> <br/><br/><i>“You are the most honest, good thing that I've ever had. I won't deny it to anyone.”</i><br/><br/><b>My Sal & Rey❤</b><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1552853691i/27221043._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1552715083i/27212649._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><i>
  <b>“You are my equal, my partner, my teammate, my best friend.”</b>
</i><br/><br/>This is my very first <i>Marinna Zapata</i> book. There are so many amazing reviews for this book, I was really excited to dive in, but it kinda left me drowning. I didn't HATE it, not at all, but I can't say I love it either. It was ridiculously freaking long <i>(like 16 hours and 13 minutes to be exact)</i> especially</span>
  <span id="freeText2771322427762954777" style="display:none"><b>
  <u>3 German Chocolate Cake ★'s</u>
</b> <br><br><i>“You are the most honest, good thing that I've ever had. I won't deny it to anyone.”</i><br><br><b>My Sal &amp; Rey❤</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1552853691i/27221043._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1552715083i/27212649._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>
  <b>“You are my equal, my partner, my teammate, my best friend.”</b>
</i><br><br>This is my very first <i>Marinna Zapata</i> book. There are so many amazing reviews for this book, I was really excited to dive in, but it kinda left me drowning. I didn't HATE it, not at all, but I can't say I love it either. It was ridiculously freaking long <i>(like 16 hours and 13 minutes to be exact)</i> especially when 65% of the book nothing really happens. Seriously <i>Zapata</i> could have easily cut half the book out and it would have made all the difference. Plus it really could have used more editing. <i>Kulti</i> is a slow burn romance and when I say "slow burn" I mean it was a Sloooowwww burn romance if you can even call any of what happened romance. There was also far too much soccer-speak for my liking. <br> <br><i>
  <b>“This is what matters. You are my gift, my second chance, and I will cherish you and your dream. I will protect both of you.”</b>
</i><br><br>Some of the things that really drove me crazy are the overabundance of using the same words over and over again. There were pages upon pages of the word "poop" and a tone of food names. It was a little funny at first but honestly, it was annoyingly excessive. <br><br><b>
  <u>To name a few:</u>
</b><br>•Poop •The German •Brautwurst •Saurkraut •German Chocolate Cake •Pumpernickel •Reindeer •German dingle-berry •German Tank • Berlin •Rey •Taco •Schnecke❤ (and so many more). <br><br><b>
  <i>“You don’t get to live your dreams by waiting around for someone to hand them to you.”</i>
</b><br><br><u>My favorite character</u> in this entire book would absolutely have to be Sal's father. He was such a loving, hilarious and really such an incredible character. None of the other family members stood out, they just faded into the background because really Sal's father was the light in the midst of dull moments for me!<br><br><u>Sal is the kickass main female character</u>. I did like her for the most part. I love the way she stood up for what she believes in and the way she defends the people she loves. But she also came across really immature for being a 27 year old and it was really annoying/childish that every time she found herself checking Kulti out she literally thought of poop or him pooping. It was... Weird. Disgusting. and to be frank it was absurd. <br><br><u>As for the main male character</u>, Kulti was a complete and utter ASSHOLE! He was self-important, rude to everyone, self-indulgent, brooding, quiet, emotionally unstable and an all-around douchebag. But hey apparently it's cool because he's like super HOT and the "King" of soccer. Yadda yadda yadda. I also felt that he has the least character development throughout. So yeah I didn't really care for him. At all, if I'm being honest. <br><br>As for their so-called connection. I just didn't get it nor did they truly have that great of chemistry. But maybe I missed it with all the repetition and me not caring for the hero. ¯\_(ツ)_/¯ <br><br>Another thing I'd like to mention is my disappointment that Sal's brother Eric NEVER makes an appearance. Yet apparently they are super close and talk to each other ALL THE TIME. But nope. Nothing. Nada. Zero. Ziltch. <br><br>If I look past all of the things that bugged me about this book, I can say it was okay. I did enjoy the second half of the story. Still didn't love it (obviously) but it did have some good parts. <br><br><i>
  <b>“You are the least shameful thing in my life.”</b>
</i><br><br><b>Would I recommend this book?</b> No probably not. Then again I know a lot of people love the shit outta it. So...maybe? <br><br><b>Do I intend on reading another book by this author?</b> Hmm. I'm not totally sure. Perhaps in the future. I don't wanna write her off just get. <br><br><i>*I should mention that Callie Dalton (The Narrator) did a fantastic job!!! If your planning on reading this I definitely recommend the audiobook version.*</i><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1552715083i/27212649._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>You’re supposed to protect what you love, Sal. You taught me that. I didn’t wake up one day and know I didn’t want to live without your horrible temper. I saw so much of me in you at first, but you aren’t like me at all. You’re you, and I will go to my grave before I let anyone change any part of you. I know that without a doubt in my mind. This,” he pointed between us. <b>“This is what matters.”</b></i><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1552883795i/27222033.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>“You are my best friend, my love, my playmate and my teammate. You’ll have a team with me wherever we are, with whatever we are playing.”</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="2771322427762954777" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer3631335918241665240"><blockquote><b>The Wall of Winnipeg and Me was my first book by Mariana and after reading Kulti, I am now convinced the author is the queen of slow-burn romance but not entirely in a good way.</b><br/><br/>As with TWOWAM, this book also has a brooding H who basically broods for no apparent reason. Nothing wrong with the strong silent type but jeez Louise, must they also be douche-bags? Further, the MCs in both books were just annoying and had zero character development and I honestly couldn't care less about Sal, the h in K</blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText3631335918241665240" style="display:none"><blockquote><b>The Wall of Winnipeg and Me was my first book by Mariana and after reading Kulti, I am now convinced the author is the queen of slow-burn romance but not entirely in a good way.</b><br /><br />As with TWOWAM, this book also has a brooding H who basically broods for no apparent reason. Nothing wrong with the strong silent type but jeez Louise, must they also be douche-bags? Further, the MCs in both books were just annoying and had zero character development and I honestly couldn't care less about Sal, the h in Kulti, who has to be the most insipid, Milquetoast female character ever.<br /><br />How could she have been so physically strong yet have such low self-esteem? Her whole being was a statement in incongruity. I really disliked the way she never ever rocked the boat but just accepted crap treatment from every and anyone. ARRRRRGGGGHHHH!<br /><br /><b>Gosh I am conflicted and have developed unreserved antipathy towards the author's style of zero emotions/kissing/sex (until the 90% mark) and to be honest, I'm not sure Kulti and Sal deserve their HEA.</b><br /><br />In a nutshell, I felt the story was parochial, predictable, had too much soccer-speak (IMO) and for a book of 570 pages, I think only 200 pages or so are relevant. My chest burns.</blockquote></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48727754-chan?shelf=all-time-faves">all-time-faves</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48727754-chan?shelf=age-gap">age-gap</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48727754-chan?shelf=book-bfs">book-bfs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48727754-chan?shelf=2017">2017</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2078834348" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8322806191942466492">5 fucked-me-right-up stars<br/><br/><i>“He was my coach. And I was his friend. Or something like that.”</i><br/><br/>this book was fcking EVERYTHING to me. in typical zapata fashion, this was a sloooooow burn romance between professional soccer player Sal & her coach Reiner Kulti. Rey is a renowned soccer star & was someone that Sal looked up to long before he became her coach. and of course she's had a crush on him since she was a kid.<br/><br/>thankfully Rey doesn't give a shit and does not return those warm feelings, at least in</span>
  <span id="freeText8322806191942466492" style="display:none">5 fucked-me-right-up stars<br /><br /><i>“He was my coach. And I was his friend. Or something like that.”</i><br /><br />this book was fcking EVERYTHING to me. in typical zapata fashion, this was a sloooooow burn romance between professional soccer player Sal &amp; her coach Reiner Kulti. Rey is a renowned soccer star &amp; was someone that Sal looked up to long before he became her coach. and of course she's had a crush on him since she was a kid.<br /><br />thankfully Rey doesn't give a shit and does not return those warm feelings, at least initially. the relationship between the two is very much coach &amp; player for the majority of the book which i loved. we get to get inside the mind of a high achieving female soccer player and understand what it takes to get to the level that she wants to be at. and what it would be like if the person you looked up to most in the world becomes your coach. and isn't all that nice to you.<br /><br />as the book progresses, obviously we get friendship stages and romantic stages and fuck i can't do it justice. but let's just say if you enjoy power play &amp; age gaps you will fucking adore this book. it was heartfelt, and even the mildly cheesy/convenient end didn't bother me. <br /><br />i don't even know what to say, just go read this.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8322806191942466492" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1506531297" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1506531297" />
    <a title="Beverly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13095060-beverly"><img alt="Beverly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1466964369p2/13095060.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1506531297?book_show_action=true">Jan 12, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beverly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beverly" href="/user/show/13095060-beverly">Beverly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1506531297" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11127226258887066455">O.M.G. this book, for real, I absolutely loved it! <br/><br/>When I started this massive audio, well by massive I mean 16 plus hours I was worried I would get bored. I thought there is no way I am going to love this, but I had to give it a shot. <b>I mean a professional soccer player and coach relationship, a 13 year age difference, forbidden love - it’s like it was written for me. </b><br/><br/><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>This was like the best dream and the worst nightmare all wrapped into one beautiful package.</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br/><br/>I quickly got lost in th</span>
  <span id="freeText11127226258887066455" style="display:none">O.M.G. this book, for real, I absolutely loved it! <br><br>When I started this massive audio, well by massive I mean 16 plus hours I was worried I would get bored. I thought there is no way I am going to love this, but I had to give it a shot. <b>I mean a professional soccer player and coach relationship, a 13 year age difference, forbidden love - it’s like it was written for me. </b><br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>This was like the best dream and the worst nightmare all wrapped into one beautiful package.</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>I quickly got lost in the world of Sal and her life as a professional soccer player. She is super talented, kind hearted and a leader to her team, but she is still just a girl. So when the love of her childhood life shows up to be the assistant coach for her team she has to constantly remind herself he is just a man to keep from swooning. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1452728751i/17734070._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Reiner Kulti, international soccer superstar, makes it pretty easy for Sal to quit swooning. He is a complete ass and it’s obvious he is miserable in his new position. It doesn’t take long for our strong heroine to infiltrate Kulti’s world and once she is in he wants more. He is drawn to the kind of person she is and just wants more. <br><br>So yeah, this audio is sixteen plus hours and most of the time Kulti and Sal are just existing together, but I freaking loved it! I loved how their relationship felt real. There wasn’t any insta-love, I felt like I was actually watching two people develop a bond that leads to falling in love. I was hooked and in love this story I didn’t even want it to end. I even teared up in the epilogue imaging these two lives together. So yeah, I sound like a complete nut and I am rambling, but shit I love this book. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1452728751i/17734071._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I am not a sports enthusiast and the only soccer I have watched is when it’s on television on Saturday mornings after cartoons. But that didn’t matter because this story is more. <b>I have no idea why this book hasn’t received the hype it deserves, it’s pretty freaking epic to me!</b><br><br>
  <a href="http://readingissexybookblog.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1423003910i/13574955.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>

<div id="review_1292498049" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1292498049" />
    <a title="Rachel Reads Ravenously" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously"><img alt="Rachel Reads Ravenously" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539149211p2/14514998.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1292498049?book_show_action=true">May 28, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel Reads Ravenously" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel Reads Ravenously" href="/user/show/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously">Rachel Reads Ravenously</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/25190482-kulti">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=ebooks">ebooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=new-adult-mania">new-adult-mania</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=sports-romance">sports-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1292498049" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18188024238101772321"><b> 3.5 Pumpernickel stars! </b><br/><br/><b> <i> "You are my best friend, my love, my playmate and my teammate. You'll have a team with me wherever we are, with whatever we're playing." </i> </b><br/><br/><a href='http://s177.photobucket.com/user/dawnygirl07/media/kulti%20collage.png.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1433225615i/15067680.png' alt=' photo kulti collage.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>At the age of 7 Sal developed a crush on a 19 year old German soccer player that would forever affect her life. Coming from a soccer family, she knew she would play but the superstar Kulti is what inspired her to go pro with the sport. Fast forward 20 years later, and Kulti is no longer Sal's idol. In fact he injured her brother </span>
  <span id="freeText18188024238101772321" style="display:none"><b> 3.5 Pumpernickel stars! </b><br><br><b> <i> "You are my best friend, my love, my playmate and my teammate. You'll have a team with me wherever we are, with whatever we're playing." </i> </b><br><br><a href="http://s177.photobucket.com/user/dawnygirl07/media/kulti%20collage.png.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1433225615i/15067680.png" alt=" photo kulti collage.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>At the age of 7 Sal developed a crush on a 19 year old German soccer player that would forever affect her life. Coming from a soccer family, she knew she would play but the superstar Kulti is what inspired her to go pro with the sport. Fast forward 20 years later, and Kulti is no longer Sal's idol. In fact he injured her brother in another game almost ending her brothers career and her crush ended years ago when Kulti got married, breaking her very young heart. Now Sal plays for the Pipers, a pro women's soccer team and Kulti has just been named the new assistant coach.<br><br>Kulti as a coach is quite frankly, an extremely rude asshole who wants almost nothing to do with the team.<br><br><b> <i> "He could go suck a big dick. And I hoped he gagged on it." </i> </b><br><br>Sal's childhood idol doesn't live up to her expectations and she's disappointed. It isn't until Kulti really pisses her off that she lets him have it and cracks his stone cold shell. Over time the two become friends, but hanging out with her older and way hot coach brings unwanted attention to Sal. Is their friendship worth the backlash?<br><br><b> <i> “When one door closes, another one opens. I might just have to do a little breaking and entering to get the right one for me.” </i> </b><br><br><a href="http://s177.photobucket.com/user/dawnygirl07/media/sal%20running.png.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1433225615i/15067681._SX540_.png" alt=" photo sal running.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>First off, I loved Sal as the lead of a romance based novel. She wasn't the typical heroine we read in books, she's athletic, driven, and is not obsessed with fashion. In fact, her wearing jeans and a real bra and not a sports bra was her idea of dressing up. In both her jobs as a pro soccer player and a landscaper the jobs require clothing that is comfortable and easy to move in. I also loved that she came from a Hispanic background, her father from Mexico and her mother from Argentina. I cannot tell you how refreshing it is to read a romance novel that wasn't white-washed. <br><br>Sal's family was also pretty amazing, her dad and his actions around Kulti as a star struck fan had me giggling and smiling. I would have liked to know a bit more about the relationship between Sal and her sister. It was mentioned how things were strained, but never really fully explained or resolved, I'm a bit bummed that we didn't get more development in that aspect.<br><br>Also the wit and dry humor was fantastic. It too had me smiling while reading.<br><br><b> <i> "'That was my first time using a lawn mower.'<br>I fucking knew it!! I didn't say that of course, instead I stuck with a very grown up, 'Oh really?'" <br><br>"Just because I'm not attracted to women old enough to remember the last Great War, doesn't mean my list is made up."<br><br>"Below the image was an italicized caption: 'If one of these lesbos is his girlfriend, I'm gonna kill myself.'" </i> </b><br><br>I really liked the growth from hatred to friendship, but I had a bit of trouble with the friends to love part of the plot. I may be really oblivious, but other than jealousy I couldn't really see the attraction grow between the two of them. Sure they ended up being perfect for each other, but I felt like I didn't see the progression from friends to lovers. By this I mean there was no specific point where I could see the change in relationship. The author still sold it in the end, but it was kind of like something was missing.<br><br>Oh and a warning, no steam until <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ 94% in!!!!  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. I was sitting here the entire book like, "when are they going to bone??" like the weirdo perve I am, and it took a while, but it happened. This book is just more plot and character development focused, romance is almost second to that.<br><br>The book was a little longer than I would have liked, honestly the first 10% or so wasn't very interesting. But the pacing picks up and it got better, I just wish some middle had been skimmed and a little more sexy times or angst were added in instead. <br><br><b> <i> "I've been waiting, and I will keep on waiting until the time is right. You are my equal, my partner, my teammate, my best friend. I've done so many stupid things that you've made me regret-things I hope you will forgive me fore and look beyond-but this, waiting a little longer for the love of my life, I can do." </i> </b><br><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="18188024238101772321" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
